Shen Bao Circulation Library - Reading Guidance Department Edited

Reading News

Contents

1. Short Preface

2. This Week's Information

3. Announcements

4. New Book Introduction

5. Acknowledgments

6. Mail Delivery

Short Preface 208

Since the last publication of Reading News, we have received many more letters this week. Many registered readers have indeed submitted reading plans to the library, and some have raised questions to discuss with this department. They all seem very active, which shows that this is entirely out of their own initiative, not passive or forced. Readers who have not communicated with this department for a long time in the past did not know our research procedures. Now that they understand, they will no longer require us to urge them. We are very satisfied with this phenomenon and hope that other readers who have not yet written will also take the initiative and not treat us here as a school, but recognize that this is our own business, and no one else is responsible; if there is dissatisfaction with our work, it can be criticized and pointed out as much as possible. Our work is entirely based on all readers. Only when everyone raises opinions can we move forward and our work progress. On our part, we will never be "ashamed" because of your criticism, nor will we be annoyed by too many letters. On the contrary, we will only be more careful and energetic. We are afraid that everyone will be indifferent, making it impossible for us to think of a way.

In addition, many readers want us to increase the length. We have the same hope as the readers, but there are two conditions: one is that the material must be rich, and we must have achievements worth reporting to the readers; the second is that it should not affect the length of other columns in this newspaper. This aspect depends on the work of you all to provide us with more materials, and on the other hand, this department should try its best to find ways.

This Week's Information 209

This week, we should report to you:

(1) This week, we have added fifteen more reading comrades. They are participating in the research of this department.

(2) The demand to meet with this department in person is very enthusiastic. They call to ask, which is very sincere. Our designated consultation time is from 2 to 5 PM every Sunday afternoon, unless there are special circumstances. However, to have a consultation, it is necessary to submit a written request, and after this department agrees, this department will send an appointment letter. This procedure must be followed.

(3) This week, we received three letters, all hoping that we could discuss and study practical problems. Of course, reading to understand practical life is what we and the readers hope for, so we published an article "How to Study the Northeast Problem", and we intend to talk more about it in the future, as long as you can raise questions with us.

(4) Because of your efforts, our work has increased, so in addition to adding staff, we have extended the working hours by two hours.

(5) Participation in the research in this city was originally limited to readers of this library. Because we were afraid that expanding the scope too much would result in nothing being accomplished, now out-of-town readers of this newspaper often write letters requesting to participate, with sincere words, making it really unbearable for us to refuse, so now we have decided to invite them to join.

Announcements 210

You often write letters asking us to publish a combined edition of reading questions and answers, and we have now started compiling and printing it. It is expected that it will be published before April 15th this year, with approximately 80,000 to 100,000 words. The price has not yet been determined, but it will not exceed the cost price by much.

New Book Introduction 211

Recently, we bought a book called "Lectures on Economics" (written by Chen Maoyin, published by Beijing Hope Bookstore). This department feels that this book is worth introducing to you as an introductory reading material. Because it:

(1) It is a lecture style, and the writing style is simple, which suits Chinese tastes.

(2) It does not adhere to the narrative order of "Capital", but incorporates the development of economics after "Capital", allowing readers to gain a complete concept of economics.

(3) In addition to providing accurate explanations and narratives, it also criticizes various fallacies, which is the characteristic of this book. People who are generally infatuated with popular economics, or who know that it is a fallacy but do not know why, should all read this book. (However, whether this book is completely flawless, we cannot immediately draw a conclusion. Soon, this department will have a more detailed critique, and we hope that readers can also raise opinions after reading it)

Acknowledgments 212

In order to provide readers with discussion materials for practical problems, we have previously, with some embarrassment, sent letters to various famous magazine publishers, requesting donations. Now, we are grateful that they have given us face and sent many books and newspapers. In addition to including it in the thank-you note for the books and newspapers received by this library, we hereby give a general thank-you; and we hope that major newspapers and magazines will continue to provide generous donations.

Mail Delivery 213

Deng Baofu, Zhu Bin, Guo Zhao, Zou Lingyun, Jiao Haolin Sha Kao, Shou Yanqiu, Zhang Xing, Luo Anni, Ding Liju, Wang Zefan, Liu Jing, gentlemen: Please indicate the communication address so that we can reply.

Women's Tennis for the Far Eastern Games Adds One More Representative 215

Preliminary Selections in Shanghai on April 16th

Athletic Association Announces Preliminary Selection Regulations

The Chinese representatives for women's tennis at the Far Eastern Games have already been selected by the National Amateur Athletic Federation of China: Ms. Wang Chunqing and Ms. Wang Chunwei from Shanxi. It is learned that the Philippines has proposed changing the event to a championship competition. Although China has not expressed agreement, in order to prepare for any eventuality, it is necessary to prepare in advance, and the number of representatives needs to be increased. Therefore, the Athletic Association has decided to hold preliminary selections in Shanghai in addition to the two Wangs. Those who wish to participate in the competition may participate according to the following regulations:

(1) Date: Starting from April 16th.

(2) Location: Shanghai Chinese Tennis Courts.

(3) Those who wish to participate in the preliminary selections should use provinces, cities, special districts, and overseas Chinese organizations as units, and be sent and registered by the sports authorities of each unit.

(4) Registration period: From now until April 13th (based on the date the list is received).

(5) Registration location: National Amateur Athletic Federation of China, Shanghai.

(6) Preliminary selection competition method: Each match will be a best-of-three-sets system.

(7) After the preliminary selection competition, the selection committee hired by this association will select one (or two, if necessary) technically excellent player to serve as a representative to participate in the Far Eastern Games.

(8) The travel expenses to and from Shanghai and the accommodation expenses in Shanghai for the players participating in the competition shall be borne by themselves.

(9) The selected players will have their travel expenses to Shanghai reimbursed by this association.

Unfortunate Incident in Zhenjiang Sports Circles; Attempt to Assault Referee 228

Students from Leidian School Resort to Violence After Basketball Defeat

Zhou Mingzhang Escapes Through Window, Unharmed

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) During the provincial basketball championship organized by the Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Public Stadium on the 17th of this month, in a match between the Leiming team and the Xiaodao team, referee Zhou Mingzhang called a foul. With the score at 12 to 45, the Leiming team suddenly claimed that the referee was being unfair and declared their withdrawal. The next day, another match was held at the stadium, and Zhou was again present as a referee. Dozens of military students from the Dianlei School (the Dianming team belongs to this school) suddenly began to criticize Zhou. Zhou retreated to the stadium's ball-borrowing room but was pursued to the door, which was then forced open, and the students rushed inside. Seeing the situation, Zhou quickly jumped out of a window and fled. After the incident, enthusiastic sports figures in the provincial capital expressed deep regret that such actions undermine the very purpose of promoting sports. Although Officer Wang of the Dianlei School offered a verbal apology and promised to punish those responsible, the other party believes that the school authorities should take full responsibility for handling the matter. As a result, the issue remains unresolved. Consequently, those serving as referees are now wary. It has also been reported that some participants have stated that unless the school takes appropriate measures and guarantees that similar incidents will not occur again, they will withdraw from any future competitions involving the school as a form of passive resistance.

Educational News from Other Regions

Jiangning Experimental County Implements Compulsory Education 232

Over the past year, Jiangning Autonomous Experimental County has made considerable progress in increasing the number of schools and improving educational methods. Recently, the county formulated and implemented measures for compulsory education in order to earnestly promote it. School-age children (ages six to nine), older out-of-school children (ages ten to fourteen), and adult out-of-school people (ages sixteen and above) are all required to attend school. School-age children must receive four years of compulsory education. Older out-of-school children enter short-term compulsory education classes for one year. Adult out-of-school people enter public schools for four months. Short-term classes and public schools both provide two hours of instruction each day. The scope of compulsory education is based on the districts designated by each school. To facilitate implementation, each school forms a compulsory education promotion committee composed of the principal, teachers, local education enthusiasts, and relevant heads of townships and police agencies. Before the start of each academic year, the committee investigates the children and adults within the school district who should receive compulsory education. Except for those who have received equivalent education at home, those who are extremely impoverished and forced to earn a living, and those who are unable to attend school due to illness or other unavoidable circumstances, all others are notified to attend school. If parents or guardians fail to ensure enrollment within one week of the school's opening (within three days for public schools), the committee will visit and persuade them. If they still fail to enroll, the school will notify the police agency to enforce compulsory enrollment or impose a fine for abandonment of education. The fine is submitted to the county government by the police agency and stored for use as a county-wide scholarship fund. The above measures were announced and implemented by the county government yesterday, further promoting compulsory education in Jiangning.

After the formal proceedings, the chairperson delivered an opening speech, and Huang Xianzhang, a member of the preparatory committee, reported on the preparations. Chairman's Report: Chairman of the presidium Han Juemin reported that China is currently facing both internal and external troubles. The country's weakness and the nation's decline have reached an extreme. To revitalize the country and restore the nation, we must follow the instructions of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, internally eliminate the communist bandits to achieve unification, and on the other hand, promote the national rejuvenation movement, revitalize the national spirit, and promote the national culture in order to save the declining nation and survive in the world. Therefore, how to revive the nation is the most urgent task. However, who will bear this responsibility of revival other than the intellectuals? Realizing this, colleagues have organized the Shanghai Professors and Writers Association to unite and carry out the practical work of national rejuvenation. In the future, we hope that professors and writers in all provinces and regions will unite, concentrate their efforts, and work together.

Pan's Speech: Director of the Municipal Education Bureau Pan Gongzhan said in his speech that Shanghai is a cultural center, but based on past circumstances, culture and the nation have been largely unrelated. For example, (1) works with feudalistic ideas still remain in society; (2) proletarian works advocating class struggle while forgetting the nation are rampant; (3) cynical and decadent romantic works are extremely popular. Therefore, the culture needed by the entire nation is lightly sacrificed. Now, the Shanghai Professors and Writers Association, realizing this, is determined to do a disinfection job, which is truly prescribing the right medicine for the illness.

Election of Officers: Han Juemin, Huang Xianzhang, Lin Zhike, Zhu Zhangbao, Chen Gaoyong, Lu Yinquan, Jiang Zhensan, Du Gangbai, and Wang Bolun were elected as executive committee members. Meng Shouchun, Zhang Yunfu, and Tang Jinbai were elected as alternate executive committee members.

Page 14

Free Talk

On Surnames by Yu Dafu 247

The origin of surnames is, of course, as old as humanity itself. The Baihutong says: "In ancient times, the sages used pitch pipes to determine surnames...Why are there hundreds of surnames?...There are five correct sounds: Gong, Shang, Jiao, Zhi, and Yu, which are mixed and transformed. Five times five is twenty-five, which in turn produces the four seasons. Different airs and special sounds are all prepared, so there are hundreds of surnames...Why are there clan names? To value meritorious deeds and despise skills, or to clan-name after their official position, or clan-name after their job." The Tongzhi says: "Before the Three Dynasties, surnames and clan names were divided into two. Men were called by their clan names, and women were called by their surnames. Clan names were used to distinguish between noble and lowly, so the noble had clan names, and the lowly had names but no clan names. Surnames were used to distinguish between marriages, so there were distinctions between those of the same surname, different surnames, and collateral surnames. After the Three Dynasties, surnames and clan names were combined into one. In writing, the birth of a woman is a surname, so the bestowal of surnames mostly follows the female, such as Ji, Jiang, Ying, Si, Yao, Gui, Ji, Yun, Zhou, Yu, and Lao, etc." From these perspectives, surnames were originally the oldest, and they existed when the female-centered family system began; then there were clan names, which originated when there was a distinction between noble and lowly in society; later on, surnames and clan names were combined into one.

Ancient people had few teeth, so there were only hundreds of surnames. Later, the population increased, and transportation became widespread. After the Tang and Song dynasties, there were more than a thousand branches of surnames. The Hundred Family Surnames that we read in private schools when we were young, starting with the Zhao surname, everyone said that it was something from the early Song Dynasty, because at that time the Southern Tang had not yet been destroyed, and the King of Wuyue occupied the south, and his power was strong. His concubine was from the Sun clan, so the first four families of the Hundred Family Surnames were Zhao, Qian, Sun, and Li. In fact, the popular version of the Hundred Family Surnames has been simplified, and the intention is only to make it easier to read. If we talk about the surnames at that time, there would definitely not be only a hundred families.

The origin of ancient surnames and clan names was like this, so the importance of surnames and clan names in feudal society and the family system is naturally unnecessary to say. Now that we are about to break the feudal society and abolish the family system, the preservation or abolition of these surnames is of course a very worthy research question. During the May Fourth era, some people proposed abolishing surnames. Some scientists among my friends have said that after surnames are abolished, identification numbers can be used to replace names, just like patients in hospitals and police officers in Shanghai patrol stations. It is not inconvenient to use only number so-and-so to replace names. Professor Xuan Tong of Beiping also implemented this proposal. Among writers, there is even a Mr. named "Abolish Name."

Recently, because I saw the creative publication problems of Mr. He and Mr. Xu, which were very noisy, the people who defended them said that even names should be abolished, so why bother about this little thing. So I wrote this paragraph of miscellaneous thoughts.

Home of the Savages by Liu Ming 248

One autumn morning, I went with two children who grew up in the mountains to climb to the top of the mountain to visit the home of the savages.

The savages are all happy to live in those cool places on the top of the mountains. The valleys or small plains at the foot of the mountains, because they have a large amount of damp heat and miasma, are left for other ethnic groups to live in. The people of Yunnan call them mountain tops, which is not without meaning.

The houses are very small, and the two wings of the thatched eaves hang on the ground. The form of the tents inhabited by nomadic peoples is still left here. The skeletons of water buffalo heads are hung at the entrance, sometimes one, sometimes three or four, which are said to be used to ward off evil spirits.

Walking into this kind of door with water buffalo skulls hanging, I sat on the floor like a guest in a familiar savage's home. The so-called floor is only paved with reeds one by one. From below, there are often sounds of chickens flapping their wings and piglets howling; a kind of offensive smell of livestock also often permeates up through the gaps in the bamboo. The host is very old, but still healthy, because he often goes down the mountain to sell firewood and gradually became acquainted with us. He tremblingly placed a finely carved silver box in front of me and asked me to chew some betel nut and lime inside. I don't know how to chew betel nut, but I just took the silver box to look at, because in such a crude thatched house, there is such a delicate thing, which cannot but make people feel surprised. The old man probably also treasures this thing very much. As soon as the conversation started, he told me about its origin with great interest. I only understand a little of the savage language. Through his gestures and the translation of the two children, I learned that this silver box was given to him by a white man. Because when he was young, he followed the head of the mountain fortress all day long, doing service. At that time, white people came to the mountain to play and gave the headman many things, so he also got a share, which is the silver box that is now regarded as a treasure. Later, when I looked at the border treaty between Yunnan and Myanmar, I saw that this savage mountain fortress called "Hu Dong" still belonged to China in the late Qing Dynasty. Judging from the old man's age, it can be known that before this place was included in Myanmar, white people had very close contact with them.

The light in the house is very dim. After sitting for a while, I saw that there were still photos hanging in a corner. One is the majestic posture of a young soldier, with a rifle on his back and a long knife hanging on his waist. According to the old man, this is his eldest son, who is stationed in a very far place. After carefully checking the English written on it, I realized that it was sent back from the Kingdom of Mesopotamia. Another one is also a photo of a young man, but his eyebrows lack the heroic spirit, and he has no weapons either. The old man said that this is his second son who follows the foreign officials, probably a comprador or something like that.

In the mountain fortress, there are wooden two-story foreign houses, schools, churches, and post offices are all set up inside. On the veranda, between the doors, and in the windows, the white hats of the nuns and the long beards of the chubby priests often flash by. The voices of children reciting or singing loudly flow out from between the fences. I don't know why. Once I left the old man's house and saw this school, I felt that future Sol-diers and Servants were being mass-produced.

When going down the mountain, the old man sent us several huge bull belly fruits. We ate half of them on the road, and the rest were thrown into the deep valley because they became heavier and heavier.

Huangyan Folk Song by Mei Jun 249

Firewood bird, flying to the ocean,

Oxherd little brother crying for his mother.

Mother serving rice full and steady,

Step mother carrying chair, unsteady chair.

Mother's grave made on the high high mountain,

Step mother's grave made in the center of the water.

Good to plant grains in front of mother's grave,

Good to pole a boat in front of step mother's grave.

Plant a white magnolia tree on mother's grave,

Plant a stinky barrel shed on step mother's grave.

Firewood bird, flying to the ocean,

Oxherd little brother crying for his mother.

Before Leaving Lion Hill (Part Two) Cao Ming 250

I stole a glance at his face, which was using stubbornness to withstand eternal pain, and felt a little pleasure. So I quickly whipped the cow's back, pulled the rope and walked away, wandering in the southern corner of the lawn, deliberately loudly scolding the black animal I was riding. The smell of cow dung and grass wafted through people's nostrils with the evening breeze. He seemed unable to grasp my meaning behind him and sang a clumsy, teasing tune in a patient voice. The cow was full and habitually walked towards home. When I was about to leave the lawn, I turned my head and said to him, "When you see the moon peeking out from the east, come to the Wind and Rain Pavilion, okay?" The cheerful singing definitely rose up behind my head.

After dinner, my sister suppressed her smile and said to me, "Just now Deputy Huang brought news from your brother-in-law, asking us two to go to the provincial capital with him tomorrow morning. Good, let's hurry up and prepare our things."

"Hey, didn't you say a few days? ... Then, can't we go the day after tomorrow?" I clumsily made my useless request. She shook her head at me as if she understood something, and smiled slyly.

The silvery moonlight shone into the living room, pouring over the people who were busy packing things. From the mountain, there was a constant transmission of depressed and sturdy mountain songs of young men and women who were flirting. This kind of sound, like the shouting of a monster that had been pressed under the sea for a long time, pierced my ears unusually. I was about to be destroyed in anxiety and cursing! When I was free and quietly ran out, everyone had closed their doors. Probably because the mountain songs were completely silent, the moon seemed particularly desolate. I walked into the Wind and Rain Pavilion, breathed a sigh of relief comfortably, and my eyes arbitrarily searched this lonely mountain top. The lights that would not go out until the sun rose from the Lai Family Village, annoyingly flashed under the moon, like phantoms, vaguely showing that there were many sturdy figures busy working in the threshing ground, and the sound of beating rice stalks densely and suddenly stabbed my nerves, and proudly shook the entire village.

I wandered around the Wind and Rain Pavilion, and the cold dew coldly touched my skin through the thin clothes, like giving me an ominous omen. I clenched my fists, raised my head and carefully looked at the tall Lion Hill that was about to fall asleep, and slowly strolled back to the house.

For the sake of busy farming, and for the sake of threshing grain all night long with Lai Laohu, the farmhands of Lai Family Village and I will never be able to meet again.

Sketches of Beiping by Yao Ke 251

(2) Wind and Dust

Like an avalanche, sprinkled like powder in the air, the sky has turned gray-yellow丨This is the curse of Beiping丨Wind and dust. In fact, although the wind in Beiping is strong, it is far less than the hurricane in Shanghai last year. However, when Beiping people talk about the word "wind," it is as painful as when Shanghai people talk about "rent increase." This is probably because of the "dust." The wind and dust have reached a tacit understanding, and the momentum is indeed huge, which is not comparable to ordinary ones.

When the wind blows, people can hear the whistling of the wind in the house, which shakes the doors and windows. Although my houses in Beiping are tightly papered, they cannot avoid the invasion of wind and dust. In a short while, a layer of yellow-black fine dust settles on the tables and miscellaneous objects, even in the drawers, which can be said to be "penetrating everywhere!"

It goes without saying that once you go out the door. The wind helps the dust, and the dust borrows the power of the wind. The yellow dust occupies the entire space. Women use thin veils to cover their faces, and men wear windproof glasses or cover their mouths and noses with handkerchiefs, but it is still useless. Only by sitting in a rickshaw, with cotton canopies covering it tightly on all sides, can you avoid the impact of wind and dust. However, the rickshaw pullers still pull the rickshaw as usual丨although slower than usual丨According to some people, they are born with the embryo of pulling rickshaws, so they have this camel-like instinct!

However, sitting in a rickshaw with a cotton canopy only avoids the wind and dust hitting your face; the gloomy and bone-chilling cold air still seeps in through the gaps in the cotton canopy. Licking your tongue on your lips, you feel a circle of dust sticking to it. Looking forward through a small piece of glass in the car curtain, the rickshaw puller seems to be running in the wind and dust like flying through the clouds. When you pull it to your destination, jump out of the car and look at his face, you will definitely suspect that he is not the rickshaw puller just now! His face is as black as a coal store clerk, only showing a pair of black eyes and two rows of white teeth!

When the wind is blowing, the best thing to do is naturally to "sit at home behind closed doors." If you must go out, sitting in a rickshaw cannot completely block the wind and avoid the dust. The best thing is to take a car, close the car doors tightly, and wrap a fox fur car blanket around your legs, no matter how strong the wind and dust are, it will not be able to do anything!

Not only that, but even when there is no wind, taking a car and speeding on the street like flying, rolling up a gust of wind and raising half a street of dust, is also full of power. This kind of power is not available in Shanghai cars.

'Choose an auspicious day to open'

Mutterings by Xia Chang 252

(10)(3)

Gui Zhuang (Xuangong)'s "Diary of Seeking Flowers" is a wonderful work in ancient diary literature. The "Xiaoshishanfang Series" has published its complete manuscript (the initial publication does not include everything). The life of the Ming loyalists can be seen in the process of his seeking flowers. A month ago, I obtained a letter he wrote to Weng Jilin in Guiwei year, saying: "I went out in May and stayed in Jiangbei, and returned in September. The people of Kunshan were all surprised when they saw me, because it had been rumored that I had died for a long time. According to the Five Elements Chronicle, all false rumors are attributed to disasters. For example, false rumors about the Yellow Dragon Child and false rumors about the arrival of a great flood are all recorded in history. This year, there were earthquakes and floods, which are manifestations of disasters in heaven and earth. The people of Jiangnan falsely rumored that I was dead or alive, which is a manifestation of disasters in human affairs. I don't know whether today's historians should also write it down? I laugh. I once said that the oranges and tangerines of Dongting, the maple tea of Yu Mountain, and the chrysanthemums of the seashore all belong to the sacred view, and they are all in one time and place. It is difficult to get them all without the same route. When autumn and winter meet, I should moor a small boat on the river bank and let the wind blow it, east to the east and west to the west. The west wind has been tight for several days, and it will blow to the chrysanthemum bushes on the coast of the East China Sea. The red buds and red fruits in the mountains, I know they are already rotten, it's a pity that I have no chance this year, I can only dream of traveling." Not only do you see the life situation of Gui Zhuang's group of people, but the helpless and unavoidable sad and indignant mood is also a good reference for "Diary of Seeking Flowers," so I quickly recorded it.

Last Testament (6) Lin Huiyin 254

"Not yet. They're very busy, you know, they don't just have this one thing. I went a few times and said it wasn't clear. Who thought they only had this one thing to do? Didn't you say He Zhonghua's matter would be settled in just one day? But although she thought so, she didn't say it.

"I'll go ask again later," Zhuo Yun said, preparing to end this conversation.

"Sorry for the trouble. When can I get the money? Can I come get it next Monday?"

"You can get it when it's settled."

"I mean, I want to get the publication fee first on Monday."

"I'm afraid you still can't get it. Fortunately, the day is still early, today is only the 20th: it probably won't be too long," Zhuo Yun comforted.

The Monday that Yina said she wanted to get the publication fee was the day her younger brother and sister started school. If you want to go to school, you should pay the tuition first, so she really wanted to get the money that day. But she clearly saw that it was hopeless, because if she continued to say that, it might make Xi Zhuoyun feel that she was too ignorant, and say things like the right to pay the money was not in him, and he had to discuss it. So she no longer asked, and after getting his permission to "notify you as soon as it's settled," she left his office.

"This time, Xiao Ji and Xiao An will also be affected!" She thought sluggishly as she walked down the road in a daze. "I'll just make the excuse that it's the New Year and ask them to start school a few days later. Sigh, the New Year! That's right, why does the school start before the New Year? Isn't it also to collect that tuition to deal with everything at the end of the year? This end of the year is so difficult, won't anyone just stay here and not be able to get through it? If Xi Zhuoyun 丨"

Thinking of that, her heart jumped, because she knew that if the money that Xi Zhuoyun promised her became a problem, she would be one of those people who couldn't get through it.

In that unstable state, Yina only looked forward to the afternoon in the morning, and looked forward to tomorrow today, hoping that she could get the money sooner. She lived so unsteadily until the evening of the 23rd, when she received the letter from Xi Zhuoyun that she was so eagerly waiting for. In that letter, he said that the publishing house had agreed to sell the manuscript, but was only willing to add two yuan per thousand words in addition to the publication fee (in her letter, she followed his suggestion and asked to add four yuan per thousand words). Finally, he advised her to agree to it anyway.

"What's there to disagree with?" The heart that had been hanging in the air for a few days, but now had a landing, was laughing.

Securities - Last Day of March Futures - Bond Market Extremely Chaotic 260

Speculators have already emerged... various bonds fell back by 0.2 to 1 yuan

1926 Bonds are Uniquely Strong... Highest Peak Reached 12.8 Yuan

Yesterday at the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, the market was extremely chaotic on the last day of trading for March futures. The 1926 Bonds were particularly volatile. The reporter repeatedly warned that those who blindly follow will suffer losses. It was known early on that the rumors were fabricated, and that those involved would not hesitate to harm others for their own benefit. These bonds neither repay principal nor pay interest, yet rumors of consolidation suddenly caused the 1926 Bonds to surge while other bonds fell significantly. The common ignorant investor has been harmed more than once. In reality, the 1926 Bonds were issued for 96 million yuan, of which over 56 million was in Japanese currency. They have never been drawn for interest payments. Even the Japanese portion has only repaid principal three times. Before the Japanese portion can be consolidated, the domestic silver portion is of course even more out of the question. Understanding this, the repeated harm suffered by the ignorant is their own fault. Yesterday, the early session saw most bonds fall back by a small amount, from 2-3 jiao to 6-7 jiao. The 1926 Bonds remained unaffected. The Disbandment and Demobilization Bonds rose slightly due to short covering. The secondary session saw a consistent decline of around 0.5 yuan. Later, the Unified Salt Bonds remained relatively stable, while the 1926 Bonds were artificially inflated, surging by around 0.5 yuan. At the afternoon opening, various bonds rebounded by 2-4 jiao, while the 1926 Bonds suddenly surged by 0.5 to 2 yuan. At the close, various bonds fell back by 2-3 jiao to 6-7 jiao, while the 1926 Bonds fell sharply by over 1.5 yuan. This situation was obviously caused by speculators manipulating prices to prepare for an exit. As a result, the market prices ranged from 2-3 jiao to 1 yuan, while the 1926 Bonds remained up by 0.2 to 0.75 yuan. The total trading volume was approximately 30 million. The closing price was 8 p.m., so details are omitted. The results of the price increases and decreases are listed below (unit: yuan):

Cotton Yarn Warehouse Inventory Increases Daily, Marked Yarn Remains Soft 261

The yarn market remains weak, and the situation remains soft. With the surrounding environment deteriorating, factories are considering not entering the exchange, but actual market demand is sluggish. Apart from offering standard yarns for sale, there is no other solution. As a result, yarn inventories in warehouses are accumulating, with a huge 14,800 bales of new goods having already been delivered. A certain factory had a firm intention to purchase, but now, seeing the poor situation and the inability of factories to unite, it is difficult to support the overall situation alone, and they will reluctantly settle this month's quota, so the market prices are falling daily. However, the future of the cotton industry appears bleak.

Grains - Speculators Sell Off Marked Flour 268

Yesterday, the flour market showed a generally weak trend after opening in the morning for all months. Foreign wheat quotations were up approximately 0.12 yuan in Chicago and up 0.08 yuan in Canada. When prices opened, the market atmosphere was still relatively stable. However, with actual sales showing no activity, some speculators, in this environment, dared not hold on any longer and gradually sold off their positions, causing the market to become sluggish. When the afternoon market opened, the near-term and long-term situations remained unfavorable. Although factories did not release new chips, the overall domestic purchasing power was extremely weak. It was also rumored that Tianjin flour mills, with an influx of wheat from the surrounding countryside, were able to operate at full capacity, while Shanghai mills were mostly operating at reduced capacity. From this situation, it appears that the demand for Shanghai flour is facing another obstacle. As a result, the current month was down 0.0125 yuan from the previous week, April was up 0.015 yuan, May was down 0.02 yuan, June was down 0.0175 yuan, July was down 0.015 yuan, and August was down 0.02 yuan.

Wheat Market Quiet, Empty Auctions Predominate 269

Yesterday's wheat futures market remained quiet and lifeless. As the current month is approaching delivery, only the morning session saw trading, down 0.01 yuan. The afternoon saw mostly empty auctions, while other months remained at the same price, with empty auctions predominating. Although the future outlook is not good, due to the timing, both long and short positions dare not enter or exit the market. However, the current influx of spot wheat is a cause for concern for future standard prices, and changes must be observed. The spot wheat market remains stable. However, shipments from Shandong, Henan, and Gansu have all arrived, which was unexpected by the factories. The market value can be temporarily maintained due to factory demand. Dali collected wheat opened at 3.6 yuan, Huangqiao wheat at 3.6 yuan, Bengbu wheat at 3.54 yuan, Wuhe wheat at 3.54 yuan, Yingzhou wheat at 3.54 yuan, Xuzhou Yaowan wheat at 3.6 yuan, and Shandong wheat at 3.65 yuan for 3,000, totaling 14,000 bales, which were reportedly handled by Fuxin Huafeng.

Evening Rice Market Conditions – Market Goods Are Weak 270

丨Thick Japonica and All Kinds of Colors are Stable丨

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, over forty cargo ships arrived from various gangs (estimated at over 6,000 stones of goods). Due to the drizzling rain, the market sentiment stabilized slightly. Therefore, the prices for regular gangs such as Sutong and Nan'gang Japonica remained unchanged from the previous levels. Du Yangjian and Yin Bianyuan were also average. However, regarding the late rice from various gangs, the purchasing intentions of the Nan'yang gang, who had previously contracted orders, weakened and their selection criteria became more middle-to-lower grade, while the Bei'yang gang showed the opposite trend, with stronger purchasing power and selective picking of higher-grade materials. This created a market trend of increasing prices for higher grades and decreasing prices for lower grades. As a result, a total of 2,300 to 2,400 packages of Qingjiao, Songsi, and Xilian late rice were shipped by both the Nan'yang and Bei'yang gangs. The prices for high-quality goods increased by four to five cents, while middle-to-lower quality goods decreased by two to three cents.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, various goods from He'xia reached the 22nd and 23rd terms. Sales of various types of rice in the market were very slow. The price of white Japonica continued to decrease slightly by three to five cents. Yangdu, Bukejian, early thin rice, Baiyuan, and Yinyuan prices remained weak.

Customer Rice Price Decline – Sales Activation 271

Local Merchants are Attempting to Operate

Yesterday, the customer Xian rice market was initially weak due to ample inventory and continuous supply. Some goods owners urgently sought to sell, willingly lowering prices for early sales. Therefore, the asking price for various rice continued to decrease slightly by three to four cents. Local merchants began to inquire, and Wen and Yong gangs continued to attempt to handle various types of rough Xian rice. This street and Fuzhou also showed some interest. Although transactions were not booming, they had become more active. If the current handling can successfully digest the customer rice, then there should be continued sales in the future. However, the market inventory is sufficient, the supply is continuous, and the goods en route have not yet fully arrived. Therefore, hoping for a significant increase in market prices is very difficult. Yesterday, the entire city shipped 900 packages of Chenji Xian rice through this street, priced at 6 yuan 10 cents to 6 yuan 3 cents. Ningbo shipped 160 packages of Jingliu rough rice, priced at 6 yuan 5 cents. Chuzhou rough Xian rice 94 packages, priced at 5 yuan 65 cents, Wenzhou shipped 200 packages of Zaoshi rough rice, at the same price. Fuzhou shipped 160 packages of Jingjing rice, priced at 6 yuan 40 cents.

Soybean Purchasing Interest Remains Good 272

Yesterday, there was no significant change in the soybean market conditions, and the outlook was still less optimistic. As the Dalian soybean market declined, shipping to Shanghai was still able to meet sales. Therefore, the market sentiment was weak. Yesterday, a carload of large Yingzhou beans, a carload of medium-sized beans, a carload of Xuzhou beans, a carload of Feihe beans, two carloads of Bengbu beans, two carloads of Bozhou beans, a carload of Nanshaoji beans, and over 700 packages of Guide Dangshan beans were sold. The outlets include exports to Fuzhou, inland car workshops, and local factory sales.

Silk and Tea – Hangzhou and Shaoxing Spring Silkworms Begin Incubation 273

Unfavorable Weather Conditions Hinder Hatching – Sericulture in Zhejiang Province is earliest in the Hangzhou and Shaoxing regions. The Qingming Festival is approaching soon. Farmers in early sericulture areas such as Yuhang, Haining, and Chang'an in Hangzhou, and Qianshan and Xinchang in Shaoxing, are now starting to incubate silkworm eggs. The current batch of egg papers are all improved varieties sold by the Improvement Association, priced at 85 cents per sheet. However, the weather has been unstable recently, with varying temperatures, which is unfavorable for incubation. Based on the weather on the day of the Flowers Birthday yesterday (February 12th of the lunar calendar), which was cloudy with light rain, sericulture farmers predict that the silkworm harvest this spring may not be abundant.

Wuxi Stocked Silk Transported to Shanghai for Storage – Recently, silk sales overseas have been sluggish, reaching an extreme point. Wuxi manufacturers hold significant amounts of silk in stock and are suffering huge losses, making it impossible to promote sales. As spring sericulture in Zhejiang Province begins, new silkworms will soon enter the market. Manufacturers are transporting their stocked silk to Shanghai and storing it in foreign warehouses in preparation for temporarily mortgaging it to the Shanghai financial community to raise funds for purchasing cocoons. Therefore, over two hundred packages of white filature silk have been transported to Shanghai via freight cars from Wuxi in recent days.

European and American Silk Sales Have Become Stagnant – The European and American raw silk markets have recently become sluggish due to the slow sales of silk fabrics. Most silk weaving factories have reduced production or stopped operations. Currently, silk factories face sluggish sales, and silk prices have plummeted. Foreign firms in Shanghai do not dare to risk purchasing raw silk, while Chinese silk merchants cannot promote sales due to significant losses. Domestic silk factories also have no interest in purchasing. The silk market has become stagnant. Yesterday, only Dafeng and others purchased five packages of white filature and ten packages of grey filature at declining prices.

Flourishing Tea Industry in Hunan and Hubei 274

Since 1925, the black tea industry in Hunan and Hubei provinces has been ravaged internally by communist bandits and externally by the encroachment of Indian tea sales. The annual export volume has decreased from 300,000 chests to 60,000-70,000 chests. Tea farmers and merchants in the region have reached the extreme of hardship. Currently, some merchants, seeing that the sales of coarse tea in England were not bad last year, have a very strong interest in Hunan and Hubei black tea. Recently, in tea-producing areas such as Anhua, Taoyuan, Changshou Street, and Niejiashi, more than thirty new tea processing plants have been established. Including the existing tea companies, there are now more than 120 in total. Tea companies in Hankou have also sent staff to the mountains to provide loans. The situation is very prosperous.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Official 293

— Autumn

I often hear people say, "The Chinese national character is 'official.'" Why is that? Because from the moment a person is born, they are related to "official." When a family has a new son or grandson, they all call him "Aguan" or "Guanguan." Even his parents and elders have to give him a nickname. The eldest is called "Daguan" (Big Official), the second is called "Erguan" (Second Official). If their Five Elements lack metal, they call him "Jinguan" (Gold Official). If his zodiac sign is a tiger, he's called "Huguan" (Tiger Official). Other names like Fuguan (Fortune Official), Shouguan (Longevity Official), Chunguan (Spring Official), Qiuguan (Autumn Official), Qianguan (Heaven Official), Kunguan (Earth Official)... the list is endless. In short, everyone loves "official." "Official" is truly welcomed!

As for families, their sole hope is that their children and grandchildren will become officials, so they can glorify the family and honor the ancestors. In society, the ultimate envy is nothing more than wanting to become an official, so they can buy land, gain power, and show off their influence. So, relatives and friends pray for nothing more than promotion and wealth; the local community worships nothing more than seeing officials taking office.

In the past, during the warlord era, people who couldn't get an official position would dream about it. Those who were obsessed with office would become "official addicts." The higher-ups sold official titles, while those below relied on the influence of officials. But it's not easy to become an official. As the saying goes, "Don't become an official unless you have someone in court." With a patron, even the most incompetent person can become an official, and they can do whatever they want without any scruples. As the saying goes, "Only the magistrate is allowed to set fires; the common people are not allowed to light lamps." They can be full of official airs and speak in official jargon, ignoring the affairs of the people, saying, "Even an honest official can't settle family disputes." Colleagues must help each other, adhering to the principle of "officials protect each other." If you don't have a strong background, you must curry favor with your superiors, otherwise, you'll be "kicked out" when a "new official takes office." The official arena is just like a theater; who goes on stage without eventually stepping down? Occasionally, there are one or two who are relatively honest, and they are hailed as good officials, like living Buddhas for the people, with their praises sung far and wide.

Speaking of being an official, one should be upright and honest, and able to adhere to official principles to deserve the position. It's just that the officials we usually see are mostly corrupt, incompetent, plague-like, and muddleheaded, so good officials are all the more rare and precious.

Officials have an official air, and officials have an official addiction. To taste the official flavor, one must drill and scheme to get it. To indulge in the official addiction, one must boast and flatter to achieve it. So, lawyers don't want to be lawyers, they want to be judges; doctors don't want to be doctors, they want to be medical officers; policemen want to be police officers, soldiers want to be military officers. Other banks have directors, post offices have postal officials, even guards have guards officers, and secretaries have secretarial officers. Whether they are scholars, farmers, artisans, merchants, soldiers, or police, everyone wants to be an official. Even the smallest official, the so-called "sesame seed and mung bean official," must be an official for the sake of being an official, to feel satisfied. Once an official position is obtained, it doesn't matter about academic qualifications, talent, or knowledge. As long as one has good official luck, even if you "mumble three garbled official scriptures," you'll still spread official reputation and climb the official ladder. That's why everyone wants to be an official.

Recent Trends in Literature and Art 294

— Shiyun

Recently, the direction of literature and art has quickly shifted to national literature. Originally, the direction of literature and art should follow the wheel of the times, and any literature and art that doesn't fit the times will inevitably be eliminated.

In the past, many of the literary and artistic creations we saw were mostly decadent, licentious, romantic, and proletarian literature with the implication of inciting class struggle. This kind of poison flowed into society and once anesthetized a part of the people, but in today's China, the rural economy is on the verge of collapse, and the social economy is showing signs of disintegration. Unless the internal groups are united and work together in production, the entire nation will be in danger. Therefore, decadent licentious, romantic, and proletarian literature can only decline with the wheel of the times.

In the past, some people advocated national literature, hoping to stand out in this tide of decadence, licentiousness, romance, and proletarianism, but the ideal and the reality were the opposite. As a result, it only appeared briefly and disappeared, but I always believed that national literature would be revived one day. Sure enough, national literature has recently become the darling of the times. This is because everyone knows that China has been deceived by imperialists, and only a strong nation can compete with others in the world. The current era is to awaken the resonance of the entire nation and work together to revive the nation's domestic production, so naturally, national literature should emerge in response to the times.

May literature revive the decline of the past eight generations. I hope that young people standing in front of the times will work hard to become the Han Yu of the modern era!

Study of Inkstones (10) 295

— Wuliao Ke

Overview of Duan Inkstones

(D) Sky Blue: Previous people only discussed sky blue by saying that it should be clear and flawless, excelling in beauty with a blue color, like the clear blue sky after autumn rain. Generally, it is like the sky blue color of porcelain after rain. Or it is said to be like the first stars disappearing in the morning, and the rising sun not yet appearing, with a quiet and profound beauty; or it is said to be like looking at the sky from afar, clear both inside and out. These are just descriptions based on each person's perspective, and there is no fixed color. However, the Japanese strongly divide it into three types:

(1) Like sky blue after rain, with a blue sky color seen faintly from light purple, it is an unparalleled masterpiece;

(2) Slightly red-blue color, like the dawn sky mixed with red;

(3) Slightly purple-gray-blue, like the twilight sky when the sun has set and the stars have not yet appeared.

As for the names "dawn sky blue" and "dusk sky blue," we have not yet been able to confirm that they are definitive. However, it is certain that sky blue has rouge-colored fire patterns and flowing cloud spots, which may be scattered or formed into pieces. Today, people often think that an inkstone that is entirely blue-purple, like the sky-blue satin color from the past, is sky blue. In fact, this kind of purple color is the natural color of the Old Pit Duan stone, not sky blue. Sky blue must be like the white of banana leaves, with colors of clouds and rainbows around it, which is the genuine article. However, it is very difficult to determine which is dawn sky blue or dusk sky blue. Wu Shihua said that blue flowers are the glory of the stone, fish brain banana white is the marrow of the stone, and sky blue is the flesh of the stone. The difference between marrow and flesh is only in the spirit and charm, without much difference, so it is listed as a beautiful pattern with fish brain banana white.

Mr. Xu Xiuzhi, a contemporary collector and connoisseur of inkstones, gave me a sky blue inkstone last year, with blue flower rouge halo, which is indeed a top grade. However, it is still impossible to determine whether it is dawn sky blue or dusk sky blue.

Biography of Auntie Back Building 296

— Chen Liang

Many times, many times, I wanted to write a short biography for someone.

After all, my friends, my relatives, my... are not qualified. Writing a biography without finding the protagonist of the biography is also a troublesome thing.

Therefore, I had to lower my standards and found "Auntie Back Building."

Auntie Back Building has no surname, no name, and is so named because she is young and lives in the back building.

Speaking of her appearance, although not very prominent, it is not bad either. She has a plump face, a big nose, thick lips, and broad front teeth. As for her eyes, when opened, they are like copper bells, and when squinted, they are like a line. She looks at people out of the corner of her eye, creating a natural charm. The source of the essence of her face lies here.

However, Auntie Back Building is not satisfied with this. Snow cream, cologne, rouge (Note: Her rouge is a corner of red paper) is applied and applied again, until she is beautified to the point where "from afar, she looks like a celestial maiden, and up close, she resembles a living ??".

"Auntie Back Building" claims to be from the other side of the Yangtze River in Jiangnan, and her Shanghai dialect is mixed with some local accent, which is melodious and amusing. She loves to gamble and does not distinguish between day and night, neglecting sleep and meals. Her husband sometimes comes home and has to "cook his own meals," make tea, wash dishes, and mop the floor. But Auntie Back Building still cannot forgive her husband when she finds a dishwashing brush bristle in her vegetable bowl or a brick piece in her rice bowl.

One evening, perhaps because she had a sudden "whim," she suddenly ran into my front building, which could not help but make me flustered, which could not help but make me drop my pen and stand up. I stole a glance at her face, which had a man-eating smile. "Uh... Sister-in-law... Is there anything... wrong?"

"See Mr. Chen's room." She said, and then looked around.

Seeing that I would not greet her, she went out. "Hehe! Mr. Chen eats tender things."

My fright settled, I smoked a cigarette, and then wrote "Biography of Sister-in-Law Back Building" to pass it on to posterity.

Northeast Four Company Commanders 297

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Six: Generously Baring His Heart, Forgetting His Family to Serve the Country; Sadly Facing the Jade Mirror, Sighing for My Beloved

When the two men peered outward through the hole in the wall, it was Guan Yaowu and Yin Deren standing together in the open space, talking. So the two men also walked out and stood in the same place. Zhao Ziqiang laughed: We men are all unsettled, only Second Brother Yin is good, he’s a bachelor. Yin Deren stuck his hands in his pockets, hopped twice, and laughed: Being a bachelor is good but when you get old, or if you get sick, that would be a little bit troublesome. Guan Yaowu said: Do you like having a family? Let’s trade places, whoever doesn’t want to switch is not human. Yin Deren spat and laughed: It’s hard for you to be an older brother, how can you say such things? If your sister-in-law was here, she might just slap you twice. Guan Yaowu had nothing to say, and shrugged his shoulders twice. Tian Qing laughed: I think Brother Guan, your marriage must have been arranged by your parents, through a matchmaker. Guan Yaowu heard these words and perked up with interest, shaking his head: No, if we were to use a new term, your sister-in-law and I even went through a passionate romance, you could say it was a free marriage, right? You Qing said: This is really fresh, our Brother Guan, had a free romance. We want to hear about it. Guan Yaowu stretched out his thumb, straightened his waist, and said: That’s for sure. Your sister-in-law and I are even cousins, and we have had feelings for each other since we were children. Although I didn’t thoroughly understand Confucius's Analects and Mencius in private school, I did like to read novels, like how Lin Daiyu and Jia Baoyu are cousins who long for each other, I know about that. Naturally, we followed that path. Tian Qing said: In that case, our sister-in-law was Lin Daiyu back then, and Brother Guan was Jia Baoyu. Saying this, he stood next to him, half-squatted down, put one hand on his shoulder, and the other on the back of his foot to compare, and laughed: What a big Jia Baoyu. This caused everyone in the field, including Guan Yaowu, to laugh. Yin Deren said: That kid is just mischievous like that. (346)

Short Story

Burial of My Child 298

— Zhu Jian

In the early summer of the twentieth year, Yuer, the only fruit of my marriage, was snatched away by death due to measles. Now, in the blink of an eye, it has been almost two years, but Yuer's lovely face and pleasant voice are still lingering in my mind, constantly. At this time, when a poor couple is cold-heartedly facing each other, I think of the joy that Yuer brought me when he was alive, and I cannot help but sadly shed tears.

This is truly a tragic scene. In that busy period of silkworm farming, my wife helped her parents raise silkworms, doing the work of picking mulberry leaves and feeding them. She was busy all day long, and I had a bout of coughing up blood because I ate fermented rice wine. Therefore, Yuer contracted measles and was initially left at his parents' home, practically leaving it to nature and not taking it seriously. Only when the illness worsened did we hire a cheap doctor to diagnose the illness. However, after taking the medicine, not only did it not improve, but also because of the superstition of the old saying that measles would be cured by sweating, medicine was boiled next to the sickbed. The upstairs in early summer was already very hot, and with the added heat of the charcoal fire, it was even more unbearable. Yuer's weak body was forced into a state of dizziness due to the hot fire.

My wife initially feared that I would be anxious during my illness, so she concealed Yuer's condition. It was not until this time that she told me the truth. Pitifully, when I heard the news, I rushed to my parents-in-law's house. My plump and lively Yuer had become so thin that he looked like a different person. His breath was wheezing, his eyes were half-open and half-closed, and the sound of phlegm in his throat was rattling. I could not help but feel a surge of bitterness rising from the bottom of my heart, floating to my nose and to my eyelids. I touched his hot head with my hand and tremblingly called "A Yuer!" When Yuer heard me, he opened his tired little eyes and looked at me, and a sound of "Papa!" burst out of his rattling throat. The tears I had tried so hard to hold back could not help but fall straight down. Alas! Yuer's illness had already reached a very dangerous point, but my finances were originally limited. At that time, I was taking medicine because of my coughing up blood and felt it difficult to manage, so although Yuer's illness was unusually severe, I was unable to hire a doctor to come and treat him. I could only wrap Yuer up and carry him to the doctor's door to be examined. Yuer's illness was originally extremely vicious, and with the added burden of running around in the wind, the precious medicines such as "Antelope Horn Powder" and "Pearl Yellow Powder" were taken, and the Western medicine ointment was wrapped on his body, but finally, it had no effect. Yuer's little life finally faded away on a bleak morning.

That tragic situation is truly unbearable to recall! I remember that when my wife and I were at the doctor's door and were rejected by the doctor, when a glimmer of hope was completely extinguished, my wife held Yuer and sat in a rickshaw, and I followed behind the car and returned home. Yuer's breath became louder and louder, and his teeth were also clenching with a rattling sound, but when he was hugged into the room, his little eyes, which had been closed for a long time, suddenly opened and looked around, revealing a reluctant expression. My wife held him in her arms and could not help but cry sadly, and I also cried aloud. Although Yuer's breath gradually weakened, his open eyes, besides bursting out tears, were still wide open and unwilling to close. Yuer was indeed reluctant to leave his poor parents, but I was unable to hire a famous doctor to save this weak little life because of financial constraints. My wife and I sat on either side of the cradle, crying and watching his little soul fade away.

At that time, I could not bear to bury this bit of flesh and blood in the public cemetery, so I temporarily placed him in the funeral parlor, preparing to return him to the family cemetery in winter. However, in the winter, the national crisis of January 28th, following the September 18th Incident, suddenly descended upon us. In that era of war and danger, the burial was put on hold. Then I suffered another bout of typhoid fever. The movie theater that I relied on for a living was also sold entirely due to poor business. I struggled to make a living in an unemployed environment, and my finances became even more difficult. Therefore, Yuer's burial was put on hold until last year when I found a job as an editor at a newspaper. In an environment of extreme austerity, I saved 30 yuan, so on the day of the Double Tenth Festival's holiday last year, my wife and I went to the grave, talked to the grave keeper about the cost of burying Yuer and the date, and decided to prepare to bury Yuer, to end a long-held worry.

Because my coughing up blood relapsed, the burial fee became the medicine fee, but since the burial had already been agreed upon, it was difficult to change the agreement. I managed to scrape together 20 yuan in the midst of difficulties. In that cold winter, on the desolate side of the ancestral cemetery, I watched as the small coffin was buried in the mound of yellow earth. My wife's crying shook the forest, the wind roared, people wept, my eyelids were attacked by sourness, and slowly filled with hot tears. The surrounding scenery gradually, gradually, changed from clear to a blurry mess.
